# XRefs — Component Families & Attributes

This document lists every component family supported by the cross-reference matching engine, along with all attributes (matching rules) evaluated for each family. It is generated directly from the live logic tables.

- **Generated:** 2026-06-29
- **Total families:** 43
- **Total attributes across all families:** 823

## How to read the "Match Logic" column

| Logic Type | Behavior |
|------------|----------|
| Identity | Exact match required (after normalization / aliases) |
| Identity range | Replacement value range must overlap the original's range |
| Identity upgrade | Match or a strictly superior variant per a defined hierarchy |
| Identity flag | Boolean gate — if the original requires it, the replacement must have it too |
| Threshold | Numeric comparison: replacement ≥, ≤, or range ⊇ original |
| Fit | Physical/dimensional constraint — replacement must fit (≤) |
| Application review | Cannot be automated; flagged for human review |
| Operational | Non-electrical info (packaging, supply-chain) |
| Vref check | Cross-attribute Vref→Vout recalculation with ±2% tolerance |

**Weight** is the rule's relative importance (0–10) used in scoring.

## Family Details

### 12 — Ceramic Capacitors – MLCC (Surface Mount)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 14
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for MLCC replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Capacitance | `capacitance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | A 100nF capacitor must be replaced by a 100nF capacitor. Ensure values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. MLCC pad geometries differ across sizes and are not interchangeable without a board redesign. |
| 3 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage. Caution: higher voltage-rated MLCCs may exhibit different DC bias derating. |
| 4 | Dielectric / Temperature Characteristic | `dielectric` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 9 | Dielectrics have a strict hierarchy. Class I (C0G/NP0) is most stable. You can upgrade (X5R→X7R) but never downgrade (C0G→X7R). _(Hierarchy best→worst: C0G > X7R > X7S > X6S > X5R > Y5V > Z5U)_ _(Aliases: C0G≡NP0)_ |
| 5 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. ±5% can replace ±10%, but not vice versa. Common: ±20%(M), ±10%(K), ±5%(J), ±2%(G), ±1%(F). |
| 6 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 8 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating range of the original. |
| 7 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 6 | Critical for tight enclosures, stacked PCBs, and low-profile designs. A taller part may not fit. |
| 8 | ESR | `esr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower ESR is generally better for decoupling and filtering. Exception: some resonant/EMI filter designs require specific ESR. |
| 9 | ESL | `esl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower ESL improves high-frequency decoupling. Reverse-geometry packages have significantly lower ESL. |
| 10 | Flexible Termination | `flexible_termination` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | If original requires flex termination, replacement must also have it. Required on flex-rigid PCBs and large packages prone to flex cracking. |
| 11 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 4 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 12 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive/high-reliability. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 13 | DC Bias Derating | `dc_bias_derating` | Application review (manual) | 7 | Class II MLCCs lose significant capacitance under DC bias. Different manufacturers can derate differently. Consult DC bias curves. |
| 14 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |

### 13 — Mica Capacitors (Silver Mica)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 13
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Derived from MLCC with mica-specific simplifications for precision applications

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Capacitance | `capacitance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | A 100nF capacitor must be replaced by a 100nF capacitor. Ensure values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. MLCC pad geometries differ across sizes and are not interchangeable without a board redesign. |
| 3 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage. Caution: higher voltage-rated MLCCs may exhibit different DC bias derating. |
| 4 | Dielectric Material | `dielectric` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Silver Mica dielectric must match exactly. No Class I/II hierarchy applies — mica is a distinct material class. _(Aliases: C0G≡NP0)_ |
| 5 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Mica capacitors typically have very tight tolerances (≤1%). Precision is a primary reason for choosing mica. Tighter is always acceptable. |
| 6 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 8 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating range of the original. |
| 7 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 6 | Critical for tight enclosures, stacked PCBs, and low-profile designs. A taller part may not fit. |
| 8 | ESR | `esr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower ESR is generally better for decoupling and filtering. Exception: some resonant/EMI filter designs require specific ESR. |
| 9 | ESL | `esl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower ESL improves high-frequency decoupling. Reverse-geometry packages have significantly lower ESL. |
| 11 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 4 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 12 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive/high-reliability. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 14 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |
| 15 | Temperature Coefficient | `temperature_coefficient` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Typically ±50 ppm/°C or better. Primary reason for choosing mica over ceramic. Lower TC is always better for stability. |

### 52 — Chip Resistors (Surface Mount)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 13
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for chip resistor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Resistance | `resistance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Resistance must match exactly. A 10kΩ resistor must be replaced by a 10kΩ resistor. Ensure E-series values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. 0402, 0603, 0805 etc. have different pad geometries and are not interchangeable without a board redesign. |
| 3 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. ±1% can replace ±5%, but not vice versa. Common: ±5%(J), ±1%(F), ±0.5%(D), ±0.1%(B). |
| 4 | Power Rating | `power_rating` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same power dissipation. A higher power rating is always safe. Derating curves may differ between manufacturers. |
| 5 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | The replacement must handle at least the same working voltage. Higher rated voltage is always acceptable. |
| 6 | Temperature Coefficient (TCR) | `tcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | Lower TCR means better stability over temperature. ±25ppm/°C is better than ±100ppm/°C. Critical for precision analog circuits. |
| 7 | Composition / Technology | `composition` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 5 | Thin Film offers better precision, lower noise, and tighter TCR than Thick Film. Upgrading from Thick to Thin Film is always acceptable. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Thin Film > Thick Film)_ _(Aliases: Thick Film≡Metal Glaze/Thick Film≡METAL GLAZE/THICK FILM≡厚膜≡厚膜电阻; Thin Film≡薄膜≡薄膜电阻)_ |
| 8 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 9 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Critical for tight enclosures and stacked PCBs. A taller part may not fit. |
| 10 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 3 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 11 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 12 | Anti-Sulfur | `anti_sulfur` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | Anti-sulfur resistors use special electrode materials to resist sulfur corrosion. Required in harsh environments (industrial, automotive). If original has it, replacement must too. |
| 13 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |

- **Attributes (rules):** 16
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Derived from chip resistors with through-hole mounting additions

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |

| 3 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. ±1% can replace ±5%, but not vice versa. Common: ±5%(J), ±1%(F), ±0.5%(D), ±0.1%(B). |
| 4 | Power Rating | `power_rating` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same power dissipation. A higher power rating is always safe. Derating curves may differ between manufacturers. |
| 5 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | The replacement must handle at least the same working voltage. Higher rated voltage is always acceptable. |
| 6 | Temperature Coefficient (TCR) | `tcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | Lower TCR means better stability over temperature. ±25ppm/°C is better than ±100ppm/°C. Critical for precision analog circuits. |
| 7 | Composition / Technology | `composition` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 5 | Thin Film offers better precision, lower noise, and tighter TCR than Thick Film. Upgrading from Thick to Thin Film is always acceptable. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Thin Film > Thick Film)_ _(Aliases: Thick Film≡Metal Glaze/Thick Film≡METAL GLAZE/THICK FILM≡厚膜≡厚膜电阻; Thin Film≡薄膜≡薄膜电阻)_ |
| 8 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 9 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Critical for tight enclosures and stacked PCBs. A taller part may not fit. |
| 10 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 3 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 11 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 12 | Anti-Sulfur | `anti_sulfur` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | Anti-sulfur resistors use special electrode materials to resist sulfur corrosion. Required in harsh environments (industrial, automotive). If original has it, replacement must too. |
| 13 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |
| 14 | Lead Spacing / Pitch | `lead_spacing` | Identity (exact match) | 7 | PCB hole pattern must match. Common pitches: 7.5mm, 10mm, 12.5mm, 15mm. Not interchangeable without board rework. |
| 15 | Mounting Style | `mounting_style` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Must be axial through-hole. Cannot substitute SMD for through-hole or vice versa without PCB redesign. |
| 16 | Body Length × Diameter | `body_dimensions` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Physical clearance verification. ¼W ≈ 6mm body, 2W ≈ 15mm+ body. Replacement must fit available board space. |

### 54 — Current Sense Resistors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 16
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Derived from chip resistors with tightened precision and current-sensing additions

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Resistance | `resistance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Resistance must match exactly. A 10kΩ resistor must be replaced by a 10kΩ resistor. Ensure E-series values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. 0402, 0603, 0805 etc. have different pad geometries and are not interchangeable without a board redesign. |
| 3 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 9 | Current sense resistors require ≤1% tolerance for accurate measurement. Tighter tolerance is always acceptable. |
| 4 | Power Rating | `power_rating` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same power dissipation. A higher power rating is always safe. Derating curves may differ between manufacturers. |
| 5 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | The replacement must handle at least the same working voltage. Higher rated voltage is always acceptable. |
| 6 | Temperature Coefficient (TCR) | `tcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 8 | TCR must be ≤50 ppm/°C for measurement stability. Metal strip/element types preferred over thick film. |
| 7 | Composition / Technology | `composition` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 5 | Thin Film offers better precision, lower noise, and tighter TCR than Thick Film. Upgrading from Thick to Thin Film is always acceptable. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Thin Film > Thick Film)_ _(Aliases: Thick Film≡Metal Glaze/Thick Film≡METAL GLAZE/THICK FILM≡厚膜≡厚膜电阻; Thin Film≡薄膜≡薄膜电阻)_ |
| 8 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 9 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Critical for tight enclosures and stacked PCBs. A taller part may not fit. |
| 10 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 3 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 11 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 12 | Anti-Sulfur | `anti_sulfur` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | Anti-sulfur resistors use special electrode materials to resist sulfur corrosion. Required in harsh environments (industrial, automotive). If original has it, replacement must too. |
| 13 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |
| 14 | Kelvin (4-Terminal) Sensing | `kelvin_sensing` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Separate force/sense pads eliminate lead resistance error. If original has 4-terminal layout, replacement must too. |
| 15 | Power Rating (Pulse) | `power_rating_pulse` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | Short-duration overcurrent surge handling capability. Higher pulse power rating is always acceptable. |
| 16 | Inductance (Parasitic) | `parasitic_inductance` | Application review (manual) | 5 | Verify for high-frequency current sensing (>100 kHz). Metal strip and reverse-geometry packages have lower parasitic inductance. |

### 55 — Chassis Mount / High Power Resistors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 16
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Derived from chip resistors with high-power mounting and thermal additions

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Resistance | `resistance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Resistance must match exactly. A 10kΩ resistor must be replaced by a 10kΩ resistor. Ensure E-series values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. 0402, 0603, 0805 etc. have different pad geometries and are not interchangeable without a board redesign. |
| 3 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. ±1% can replace ±5%, but not vice versa. Common: ±5%(J), ±1%(F), ±0.5%(D), ±0.1%(B). |
| 4 | Power Rating | `power_rating` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 10 | Power rating must be ≥ original, derated at specific mounting surface temperature (e.g., 50W at 25°C case). Critical for thermal design. |
| 5 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | The replacement must handle at least the same working voltage. Higher rated voltage is always acceptable. |
| 6 | Temperature Coefficient (TCR) | `tcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | Lower TCR means better stability over temperature. ±25ppm/°C is better than ±100ppm/°C. Critical for precision analog circuits. |
| 7 | Composition / Technology | `composition` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 5 | Thin Film offers better precision, lower noise, and tighter TCR than Thick Film. Upgrading from Thick to Thin Film is always acceptable. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Thin Film > Thick Film)_ _(Aliases: Thick Film≡Metal Glaze/Thick Film≡METAL GLAZE/THICK FILM≡厚膜≡厚膜电阻; Thin Film≡薄膜≡薄膜电阻)_ |
| 8 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 9 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Critical for tight enclosures and stacked PCBs. A taller part may not fit. |
| 10 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 3 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 11 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 12 | Anti-Sulfur | `anti_sulfur` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | Anti-sulfur resistors use special electrode materials to resist sulfur corrosion. Required in harsh environments (industrial, automotive). If original has it, replacement must too. |
| 13 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |
| 14 | Mounting Style | `mounting_style` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | TO-220, TO-247, TO-263 (D²PAK), bolt-down, or clip mount. Must match exactly for mechanical and thermal compatibility. |
| 15 | Thermal Resistance (°C/W) | `thermal_resistance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Lower thermal resistance is better for heat transfer to heatsink/chassis. Directly impacts maximum continuous power. |
| 16 | Heatsink Interface Dimensions | `heatsink_dimensions` | Fit (physical ≤) | 8 | Bolt hole spacing and tab dimensions must match existing heatsink/mounting hardware. Mismatch prevents installation. |

### 58 — Aluminum Electrolytic Capacitors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 17
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for aluminum electrolytic capacitor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Capacitance | `capacitance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Capacitance must match exactly. Ensure values are normalized (µF) before comparison. |
| 2 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage. Higher voltage rating is always acceptable but may increase size. |
| 3 | Polarization | `polarization` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Polar and non-polar (bipolar) types are not interchangeable. A polar cap in an AC circuit will fail catastrophically. _(Aliases: Polar≡Polarized≡Uni-Polar≡Unipolar; Bi-Polar≡Bipolar≡Non-Polar≡Non Polar)_ |
| 4 | Mounting Type | `mounting_type` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | SMD and through-hole types are not interchangeable without PCB redesign. Snap-in vs radial lead also matters. |
| 5 | Diameter | `diameter` | Fit (physical ≤) | 6 | Must fit within the PCB footprint and available board area. Especially important for snap-in types. |
| 6 | Height | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 6 | Must fit within available vertical clearance. Electrolytic capacitors are often the tallest component on a board. |
| 7 | Lead Spacing | `lead_spacing` | Identity (exact match) | 7 | Lead spacing must match for through-hole types. Different spacing requires different PCB hole patterns. |
| 8 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Electrolytics typically have wide tolerances: ±20%(M) is most common. |
| 9 | ESR | `esr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Lower ESR is critical for power supply output filtering. High ESR causes ripple voltage and heating. |
| 10 | Ripple Current | `ripple_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | The replacement must handle at least the same ripple current. This is the #1 reliability parameter for electrolytics in power supplies. Insufficient rating causes overheating and premature dryout. |
| 11 | Impedance | `impedance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower impedance is better for filtering. Impedance at 100kHz is the standard comparison point. |
| 12 | Leakage Current | `leakage_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower leakage is better. Critical for battery-powered and standby power designs. |
| 13 | Lifetime / Endurance | `lifetime` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | Longer lifetime is always acceptable. Rated in hours at max temp (e.g., 2000h @ 105°C). The electrolyte dries out over time — this is the primary wear-out mechanism. |
| 14 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range. Every 10°C above rated temp halves the lifetime. |
| 15 | Capacitor Type / Series | `capacitor_type` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 4 | Hybrid and polymer hybrid electrolytics offer lower ESR and longer life than standard types. Upgrading is generally safe. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Hybrid > Polymer Hybrid > Low ESR > Standard)_ |
| 16 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 17 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel for SMD, bulk or ammo pack for through-hole. Ensure packaging matches production line requirements. |

### 59 — Tantalum Capacitors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 17
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for tantalum capacitor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Capacitance | `capacitance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Capacitance must match exactly. Ensure values are normalized (µF) before comparison. |
| 2 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage. Tantalum capacitors are particularly sensitive to voltage stress — derating to 50% is common practice. |
| 3 | Package / Case (EIA) | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | EIA case size (A/B/C/D/E/V) must match exactly. Different cases have different pad geometries. |
| 4 | Capacitor Type | `capacitor_type` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 7 | Polymer tantalum offers lower ESR, higher ripple current capability, and benign failure mode vs MnO₂. Upgrading from MnO₂ to Polymer is generally safe. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Polymer > MnO2)_ |
| 5 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Common: ±20%(M), ±10%(K), ±5%(J). |
| 6 | ESR | `esr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Lower ESR is better for power filtering and decoupling. ESR is specified at 100kHz typically. |
| 7 | Ripple Current | `ripple_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | The replacement must handle at least the same ripple current. Insufficient ripple rating causes excessive heating and early failure. |
| 8 | Leakage Current | `leakage_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower leakage current is better. Critical for battery-powered and low-power designs. |
| 9 | Dissipation Factor | `dissipation_factor` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower dissipation factor means less energy lost as heat. Important for high-frequency applications. |
| 10 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 11 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Critical for tight enclosures and low-profile designs. A taller part may not fit. |
| 12 | Surge / Inrush Voltage | `surge_voltage` | Application review (manual) | 6 | Surge and inrush behavior varies significantly between tantalum types. MnO₂ types are more susceptible to surge failure. Review application-specific surge requirements. |
| 13 | Failure Mode (Benign) | `failure_mode` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | If original specifies benign (open-circuit) failure mode, replacement must also have it. Critical for safety — MnO₂ tantalums can fail short and ignite. |
| 14 | DC Bias Derating | `dc_bias_derating` | Application review (manual) | 6 | Tantalum capacitors can lose capacitance under DC bias, though less severely than MLCCs. Consult manufacturer derating curves. |
| 15 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 16 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 3 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 17 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |

### 60 — Aluminum Polymer Capacitors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 17
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Derived from aluminum electrolytic with solid polymer-specific modifications

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Capacitance | `capacitance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Capacitance must match exactly. Ensure values are normalized (µF) before comparison. |
| 2 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage. Higher voltage rating is always acceptable but may increase size. |
| 3 | Polarization | `polarization` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Polar and non-polar (bipolar) types are not interchangeable. A polar cap in an AC circuit will fail catastrophically. _(Aliases: Polar≡Polarized≡Uni-Polar≡Unipolar; Bi-Polar≡Bipolar≡Non-Polar≡Non Polar)_ |
| 4 | Mounting Type | `mounting_type` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | SMD and through-hole types are not interchangeable without PCB redesign. Snap-in vs radial lead also matters. |
| 5 | Diameter | `diameter` | Fit (physical ≤) | 6 | Must fit within the PCB footprint and available board area. Especially important for snap-in types. |
| 6 | Height | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 6 | Must fit within available vertical clearance. Electrolytic capacitors are often the tallest component on a board. |
| 7 | Lead Spacing | `lead_spacing` | Identity (exact match) | 7 | Lead spacing must match for through-hole types. Different spacing requires different PCB hole patterns. |
| 8 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Electrolytics typically have wide tolerances: ±20%(M) is most common. |
| 9 | ESR | `esr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 9 | ESR is the primary reason for choosing polymer. Typical: 5–30 mΩ vs 50–500 mΩ liquid electrolytic. Lower is always better. |
| 10 | Ripple Current | `ripple_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | Aluminum polymer handles significantly higher ripple current due to low ESR. Elevated importance for power supply applications. |
| 11 | Impedance | `impedance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower impedance is better for filtering. Impedance at 100kHz is the standard comparison point. |
| 12 | Leakage Current | `leakage_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower leakage is better. Critical for battery-powered and standby power designs. |
| 14 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range. Every 10°C above rated temp halves the lifetime. |
| 15 | Capacitor Type / Series | `capacitor_type` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 4 | Hybrid and polymer hybrid electrolytics offer lower ESR and longer life than standard types. Upgrading is generally safe. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Hybrid > Polymer Hybrid > Low ESR > Standard)_ |
| 16 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 17 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel for SMD, bulk or ammo pack for through-hole. Ensure packaging matches production line requirements. |
| 18 | Conductive Polymer Type | `polymer_type` | Identity (exact match) | 5 | Different polymer types (PEDOT, polypyrrole) may have different aging characteristics and ESR temperature profiles. Match if specified. |

### 61 — Supercapacitors (EDLC / Ultracapacitors)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 18
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for supercapacitor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Capacitance | `capacitance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Capacitance must match exactly. Supercapacitors range from mF to thousands of Farads. Ensure values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage. Exceeding the voltage rating permanently damages supercapacitors. Typical ratings are 2.5V, 2.7V, 3.0V, 5.0V. |
| 3 | Technology / Chemistry | `technology` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 7 | Hybrid supercapacitors combine EDLC with pseudocapacitance for higher energy density. Upgrading from EDLC to Hybrid is generally safe if other parameters match. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Hybrid > EDLC)_ |
| 4 | ESR | `esr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 8 | Lower ESR is better for power delivery applications. ESR determines the maximum pulsed power capability and energy lost as heat. |
| 5 | Peak Current | `peak_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | The replacement must handle at least the same peak current. Important for pulse power applications like backup power and regenerative braking. |
| 6 | Leakage Current | `leakage_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | Lower leakage is better. Critical for energy harvesting and long-duration backup where self-discharge matters. |
| 7 | Self-Discharge | `self_discharge` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower self-discharge means longer energy retention. Measured as voltage drop over time. Critical for backup power applications. |
| 8 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 8 | Package must match for mounting compatibility. Supercapacitors come in cylindrical, prismatic, and coin cell formats. |
| 9 | Diameter | `diameter` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Must fit within the PCB footprint. Cylindrical supercapacitors vary significantly in diameter. |
| 10 | Height | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Must fit within available vertical clearance. Supercapacitors can be quite tall. |
| 11 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 4 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Supercapacitors typically have wide tolerances: -20/+80% or ±20%. |
| 12 | Cycle Life | `cycle_life` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | More cycles is always better. Supercapacitors offer 100K-1M+ cycles vs batteries. Critical for frequent charge/discharge applications. |
| 13 | Lifetime / Endurance | `lifetime` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | Longer lifetime is always acceptable. Rated in hours at max temp and voltage. Electrolyte degradation is the primary wear-out mechanism. |
| 14 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range. Supercapacitor performance degrades significantly at temperature extremes. |
| 15 | Capacitance Aging | `cap_aging` | Application review (manual) | 5 | Capacitance degrades over time and cycles. The rate varies by technology and manufacturer. Review end-of-life capacitance for your application lifetime. |
| 16 | ESR Aging | `esr_aging` | Application review (manual) | 5 | ESR increases over time and cycles. The rate varies by technology. Review end-of-life ESR to ensure the replacement meets application requirements. |
| 17 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 18 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel or tray required for automated assembly. Ensure packaging matches production line requirements. |

### 64 — Film Capacitors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 19
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for film capacitor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Capacitance | `capacitance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Capacitance must match exactly. Ensure values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Voltage Rating (DC) | `voltage_rated_dc` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same DC working voltage. Higher is always acceptable. |
| 3 | Voltage Rating (AC) | `voltage_rated_ac` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | The replacement must handle at least the same AC voltage. Important for EMI filtering and motor run applications. |
| 4 | Dielectric Type | `dielectric_type` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 7 | Polypropylene (PP) has lowest losses and best stability. PPS handles higher temps. PEN/PET are lower performance. Upgrading is safe (e.g., PET→PP). _(Hierarchy best→worst: PP > PPS > PEN > PET)_ |
| 5 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Common: ±20%(M), ±10%(K), ±5%(J), ±2.5%(H), ±1%(F). |
| 6 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Package must match for PCB footprint compatibility. Film capacitors come in radial, axial, and SMD packages. |
| 7 | Lead Spacing / Pin Pitch | `lead_spacing` | Identity (exact match) | 8 | Lead spacing must match exactly for through-hole parts. Different spacing requires different PCB hole patterns. |
| 8 | Self-Healing | `self_healing` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | Self-healing (metallized) film capacitors can survive localized dielectric breakdown. If original requires this, replacement must also be self-healing. |
| 9 | Dissipation Factor (tan δ) | `dissipation_factor` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower dissipation factor means less energy lost as heat. Critical in high-frequency and resonant applications. |
| 10 | ESR | `esr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower ESR is generally better. Exception: some snubber circuits require specific ESR. |
| 11 | dV/dt Rating | `dv_dt` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage slew rate. Critical in snubber and pulse applications. |
| 12 | Ripple Current | `ripple_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | The replacement must handle at least the same ripple current. Important for filtering applications. |
| 13 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 14 | Height | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Must fit within available vertical clearance on the PCB. |
| 15 | Body Length | `body_length` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Must fit within available board space. Film capacitors can vary significantly in body size. |
| 16 | Safety Rating (X/Y Class) | `safety_rating` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 9 | If original has X or Y safety rating (e.g., X2, Y2), replacement must have same or better class. Required for mains-connected EMI filtering. Safety critical. |
| 17 | Flammability Rating (UL94) | `flammability` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 7 | UL94 is categorical (V-0 / V-1 / V-2 / HB) ordered best→worst. If original requires UL94 V-0, replacement must be V-0 or better; never downgrade to V-2 or HB on safety-critical end products. _(Hierarchy best→worst: V-0 > V-1 > V-2 > HB)_ |
| 18 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 19 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel or ammo pack required for automated assembly. Ensure packaging matches production line requirements. |

### 65 — Varistors / Metal Oxide Varistors (MOVs)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 16
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for varistor/MOV replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Varistor Voltage (V₁ₘₐ) | `varistor_voltage` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Primary specification at 1mA DC. Common values: 180V, 275V, 320V, 460V AC. Must match exactly — determines clamping threshold. |
| 2 | Clamping Voltage (Vc) | `clamping_voltage` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 9 | Lower clamping voltage is better for downstream component protection. Specified at peak current (e.g., 710V at 100A 8/20µs). |
| 3 | Maximum Continuous Voltage (AC/DC) | `max_continuous_voltage` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | Maximum voltage without significant leakage or degradation. Replacement must handle at least the same continuous voltage. |
| 4 | Energy Rating (Joules) | `energy_rating` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | Maximum single-pulse energy absorption (10/1000µs or 2ms pulse). Range: 0.1J (SMD) to 1000J+ (large disc). Higher is always acceptable. |
| 5 | Peak Surge Current (8/20µs) | `peak_surge_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | Standard lightning surge waveform rating. Range: 50A (SMD) to 70,000A (large disc). Higher is always acceptable. |
| 6 | Package / Form Factor | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Radial disc (through-hole), SMD chip, or block/strap. Must match mounting style exactly — not interchangeable without board redesign. |
| 7 | Disc Diameter (Radial) | `disc_diameter` | Fit (physical ≤) | 6 | Common sizes: 5mm, 7mm, 10mm, 14mm, 20mm, 25mm, 32mm, 40mm. Larger disc = better surge handling but must fit physical space. |
| 8 | Lead Spacing / Pitch | `lead_spacing` | Identity (exact match) | 7 | Through-hole pitch: 5mm, 7.5mm, 10mm, 12.5mm. Tied to disc diameter. Must match PCB hole pattern. |
| 9 | Response Time | `response_time` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Time to begin clamping after transient. ZnO element: <25ns; with leads: <500ns. SMD faster than through-hole. Lower is better. |
| 10 | Leakage Current | `leakage_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | At maximum continuous voltage. Standard: <20µA; low-leakage: <1µA. Lower prevents thermal runaway risk. |
| 11 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | Standard: −40°C to +85°C. Replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 12 | Number of Surge Pulses (Lifetime) | `surge_pulse_lifetime` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | MOVs degrade with each surge; clamping voltage drifts lower, leakage increases. End-of-life at ≥10% voltage shift. More pulses = longer service life. |
| 13 | Safety Rating (UL, IEC) | `safety_rating` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | UL 1449 (SPD) or IEC 61643 certification. If original is certified, replacement must also be certified. |
| 14 | Thermal Disconnect / Fuse | `thermal_disconnect` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Prevents catastrophic failure (fire) if varistor overheats. Required by UL 1449 for certain applications. If original has it, replacement must too. |
| 15 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications (load dump, inductive spikes, ESD). A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 16 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel for SMD; Ammo Pack or Bulk for through-hole. Must match assembly process requirements. |

### 66 — PTC Resettable Fuses (PolyFuses)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 15
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for PTC resettable fuse replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Hold Current (Ihold) | `hold_current` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Primary specification at 25°C ambient. Too low causes nuisance tripping; too high fails to protect. Must match exactly. |
| 2 | Trip Current (Itrip) | `trip_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 9 | Minimum current triggering high-resistance state. Ratio Itrip/Ihold: 1.7–2.5×. Lower trip current = faster protection. |
| 3 | Maximum Voltage (Vmax) | `max_voltage` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 10 | HARD SAFETY LIMIT. Full circuit voltage appears across tripped device. If exceeded: arcing, cracking, permanent failure. Common: 6V, 9V, 16V, 24V, 30V, 60V, 250V. Most common substitution mistake is voltage mismatch. |
| 4 | Maximum Fault Current (Imax) | `max_fault_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | Maximum safe interruption current during dead short. Range: 5A–100A. Insufficient rating can cause permanent device damage. |
| 5 | Time-to-Trip | `time_to_trip` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Time from fault onset to high-resistance state at specified fault current. Faster is better. Depends on fault magnitude (higher current = faster trip). |
| 6 | Initial Resistance (R₁) | `initial_resistance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | Untripped-state resistance. Lower = less voltage drop during normal operation. Critical on low-voltage circuits (USB 5V, 3.3V rails). |
| 7 | Post-Trip Resistance (R1max) | `post_trip_resistance` | Application review (manual) | 5 | Resistance creeps up after multiple trip/reset cycles (50–100% increase after 100 cycles). Flag if circuit is sensitive to voltage drop (precision sensing, low-voltage). |
| 8 | Package / Form Factor | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | SMD chip (0402–2920), radial leaded, or strap/battery tab. Must match footprint and mounting style exactly. |
| 9 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | Standard: −40°C to +85°C. Hold/trip currents derate severely with temperature (60–70% at 50°C). Replacement must cover full range. |
| 10 | Power Dissipation (Tripped State) | `power_dissipation` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Lower is better. Specified as Pd at Vmax. High dissipation causes heating of adjacent components on the PCB. |
| 11 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Physical clearance verification for enclosures and stacked PCBs. |
| 12 | Endurance (Trip/Reset Cycles) | `endurance_cycles` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | Number of cycles before hold current or initial resistance drifts outside spec. Typical: 100–1000+. More cycles = longer reliable service. |
| 13 | Safety Rating (UL, TUV, CSA) | `safety_rating` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for safety-critical overcurrent protection. UL/CSA/TUV certification must be present if original has it. |
| 14 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications (USB ports, sensor circuits, communication buses). A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 15 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel for SMD; Ammo Pack or Bulk for leaded. Must match assembly process requirements. |

### 67 — NTC Thermistors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 15
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for NTC thermistor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Resistance @ 25°C (R25) | `resistance_r25` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | R25 is the primary specification. Must match exactly. Common values: 10kΩ, 100kΩ. This sets the operating point of the measurement circuit. |
| 2 | B-Value (B-Constant) | `b_value` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | The B-value defines the R-T curve shape. Even small differences in B-value cause significant temperature measurement errors. Must match within tolerance. |
| 3 | R-T Curve Matching | `rt_curve` | Application review (manual) | 8 | The full R-T curve must be compared, not just R25 and B-value. Different thermistor materials can have the same R25 and B-value but diverge at temperature extremes. Consult R-T tables. |
| 4 | R25 Tolerance | `r25_tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Common: ±5%, ±3%, ±1%, ±0.5%. Determines accuracy of the temperature reading. |
| 5 | B-Value Tolerance | `b_value_tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | A tighter B-value tolerance means a more predictable R-T curve. Common: ±3%, ±1%. Critical for precision temperature measurement. |
| 6 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Package must match. NTC thermistors come in SMD chip, glass bead, epoxy coated, and probe formats. Different packages have different thermal response. |
| 7 | Thermal Time Constant | `thermal_time_constant` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Faster thermal response (lower time constant) is acceptable. Important for applications requiring quick temperature sensing. |
| 8 | Dissipation Constant | `dissipation_constant` | Application review (manual) | 5 | The dissipation constant determines self-heating error. Different values require different current limits in the measurement circuit. Must review for specific circuit design. |
| 9 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. NTC thermistors are selected specifically for their measurement range. |
| 10 | Maximum Power | `max_power` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | The replacement must handle at least the same power dissipation. Important for inrush current limiting NTCs. |
| 11 | Application Category | `application_category` | Identity (exact match) | 5 | Temperature sensing NTCs and inrush current limiting NTCs have fundamentally different designs. They are not interchangeable. |
| 12 | Height | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 4 | Must fit within available vertical clearance on the PCB. |
| 13 | Curve Interchangeability | `interchangeability` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | Some NTC thermistors are designed as interchangeable replacements with standardized R-T curves (e.g., Murata NCP series). If original uses an interchangeable type, replacement should match the same curve standard. |
| 14 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 15 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure packaging matches production line requirements. |

### 68 — PTC Thermistors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 15
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for PTC thermistor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Resistance @ 25°C (R25) | `resistance_r25` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | R25 is the primary specification. Must match exactly. This determines the normal-state behavior of the circuit. |
| 2 | Curie / Switch Temperature | `curie_temp` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | The Curie temperature is where the PTC exhibits its sharp resistance increase. This is the fundamental switching point and must match for proper overcurrent or overtemperature protection. |
| 3 | R-T Curve Matching | `rt_curve` | Application review (manual) | 8 | The full R-T curve shape determines the switching behavior. Different PTC materials can have different transition slopes. Consult datasheets for the full curve. |
| 4 | R25 Tolerance | `r25_tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. |
| 5 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Package must match. PTC thermistors come in SMD chip, radial, and disc formats with different pad geometries. |
| 6 | Maximum Voltage | `max_voltage` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | The replacement must handle at least the same maximum voltage. Exceeding the voltage rating can cause PTC failure. |
| 7 | Maximum Current | `max_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | The replacement must handle at least the same maximum current during fault conditions. |
| 8 | Maximum Power | `max_power` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | The replacement must handle at least the same power dissipation. |
| 9 | Trip Current | `trip_current` | Identity (exact match) | 8 | For resettable fuse PTCs, the trip current must match. This is the current at which the PTC transitions to high-resistance state. |
| 10 | Hold Current | `hold_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | For resettable fuse PTCs, the hold current is the maximum current that won't trigger a trip. Higher hold current is acceptable if trip current also matches. |
| 11 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 12 | Height | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 4 | Must fit within available vertical clearance on the PCB. |
| 13 | Curve Interchangeability | `interchangeability` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | If original uses a standardized PTC curve, replacement should match the same standard. |
| 14 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 15 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure packaging matches production line requirements. |

### 69 — Common Mode Chokes / Filters

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 17
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for common mode choke replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Common Mode Impedance | `cm_impedance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The primary specification. Common mode impedance at the rated frequency must match. This determines the noise suppression capability. |
| 2 | Common Mode Inductance | `cm_inductance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | Higher common mode inductance provides better low-frequency noise suppression. The replacement must provide at least the same inductance. |
| 3 | Impedance vs Frequency Curve | `impedance_curve` | Application review (manual) | 8 | The frequency response shape determines effectiveness across the target range. Two chokes with the same rated impedance can behave very differently. Consult datasheets. |
| 4 | Number of Lines | `number_of_lines` | Identity (exact match) | 7 | Number of signal lines (2, 4, etc.) must match. Determines the pin count and circuit configuration. |
| 5 | Differential Mode Leakage Inductance | `dm_leakage` | Application review (manual) | 6 | DM leakage inductance affects signal integrity. Too much leakage attenuates the desired differential signal. Too little reduces DM noise filtering. Must review for the specific application. |
| 6 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. Common mode chokes have specific pin configurations. |
| 7 | Rated Current | `rated_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same current. Exceeding rated current causes core saturation and loss of filtering. |
| 8 | DC Resistance (DCR) | `dcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Lower DCR means less voltage drop and less power loss per line. |
| 9 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | The replacement must handle at least the same working voltage. |
| 10 | Insulation Voltage | `insulation_voltage` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | Higher insulation voltage provides better isolation between windings. Critical for safety-rated applications. |
| 11 | Application Type | `application_type` | Identity (exact match) | 5 | Signal-line (USB, HDMI) vs power-line chokes have very different characteristics. They are not interchangeable. |
| 12 | Interface Compliance | `interface_compliance` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | If original is designed for specific interface (USB 3.0, HDMI 2.1, Ethernet), replacement must also comply. Interface-specific chokes are optimized for that standard's frequency range. |
| 13 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 6 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 14 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Must fit within available vertical clearance on the PCB. |
| 15 | Safety Rating (UL/TUV) | `safety_rating` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 7 | If original has UL or TUV safety rating, replacement must also have equivalent certification. Required for mains-connected applications. |
| 16 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 17 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure packaging matches production line requirements. |

### 70 — Ferrite Beads (Surface Mount)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 14
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-11
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for ferrite bead replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Impedance @ 100MHz | `impedance_100mhz` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The primary specification of a ferrite bead. Must match the rated impedance at 100MHz. This determines the attenuation of high-frequency noise. |
| 2 | Impedance vs Frequency Curve | `impedance_curve` | Application review (manual) | 8 | Two beads with the same 100MHz impedance can have very different frequency response shapes. The impedance curve determines effectiveness across the target frequency range. Consult datasheets. |
| 3 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. 0201, 0402, 0603, 0805 etc. are not interchangeable. |
| 4 | Rated Current | `rated_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same current. Exceeding rated current causes excessive heating and impedance degradation. |
| 5 | DC Resistance (DCR) | `dcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Lower DCR means less voltage drop and less power loss. Critical for power supply rail filtering. |
| 6 | Number of Lines | `number_of_lines` | Identity (exact match) | 6 | Single-line vs multi-line ferrite beads are not interchangeable. Array types have specific pin configurations. |
| 7 | Resistance Type | `resistance_type` | Identity (exact match) | 4 | Resistive vs inductive impedance type affects the frequency response characteristic. Must match for proper EMI filtering. |
| 8 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | A tighter impedance tolerance is always acceptable. Common: ±25%, ±50% (ferrite beads have wide tolerances). |
| 9 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 6 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 10 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Must fit within available vertical clearance on the PCB. |
| 11 | Voltage Rating | `voltage_rated` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 5 | The replacement must handle at least the same voltage. Higher rating is always acceptable. |
| 12 | Signal Integrity (S-Parameters) | `signal_integrity` | Application review (manual) | 7 | For high-speed data lines, S-parameter matching is critical. Insertion loss, return loss, and eye diagram impact must be verified. Consult manufacturer S-parameter data. |
| 13 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 14 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |

### 71 — Power Inductors (Surface Mount)

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 17
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-20
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for power inductor replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Inductance | `inductance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Inductance must match exactly. A 10µH inductor must be replaced by a 10µH inductor. Ensure values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. Inductor pad geometries differ across sizes. |
| 3 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Common: ±20%(M), ±10%(K), ±5%(J). |
| 4 | Saturation Current (Isat) | `saturation_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same saturation current. Below Isat, inductance drops sharply (typically defined at 20-30% L drop). Insufficient Isat causes converter instability. |
| 5 | Rated Current (Irms) | `rated_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same RMS current. Irms is the thermal rating — exceeding it causes excessive temperature rise. |
| 6 | DC Resistance (DCR) | `dcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Lower DCR means less I²R loss and less heat. Critical for high-current power inductors. Directly impacts converter efficiency. |
| 7 | Core Material | `core_material` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 5 | Metal alloy/composite cores offer softer saturation and better thermal performance vs ferrite. Upgrade from ferrite to metal alloy is generally safe for power applications. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Metal Alloy > Metal Composite > Ferrite)_ |
| 8 | Shielding | `shielding` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 8 | Shielded is best (contains magnetic field), Semi-Shielded is acceptable, Unshielded radiates. Downgrading shielding risks EMI compliance failures. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Shielded > Semi-Shielded > Unshielded)_ |
| 9 | Self-Resonant Frequency (SRF) | `srf` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 5 | Above SRF, the inductor behaves as a capacitor. Higher SRF ensures the inductor operates properly at the switching frequency. |
| 10 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 11 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Critical for tight enclosures and low-profile designs. Power inductors vary significantly in height. |
| 12 | AC Resistance (ACR) | `acr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 4 | Lower AC resistance means less loss at the switching frequency. Important for high-frequency converters. |
| 13 | Inductance vs DC Bias | `inductance_vs_dc_bias` | Application review (manual) | 7 | Inductance drops as DC current increases. Different core materials have different L vs I curves. Ferrite has hard saturation; metal alloy has soft roll-off. Consult datasheets. |
| 14 | Construction Type | `construction_type` | Identity (exact match) | 4 | Construction (wound, multilayer, molded) affects electrical and thermal characteristics. Wound types have higher current; multilayer types are smaller but lower current. |
| 15 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 16 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 3 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 17 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |

### 72 — RF / Signal Inductors

- **Category:** Passives
- **Attributes (rules):** 19
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Derived from power inductors with RF signal-frequency priority inversions

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Inductance | `inductance` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Inductance must match exactly. A 10µH inductor must be replaced by a 10µH inductor. Ensure values are normalized before comparison. |
| 2 | Package / Case | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | The replacement must match the original footprint exactly. Inductor pad geometries differ across sizes. |
| 3 | Tolerance | `tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | A tighter tolerance is always acceptable. Common: ±20%(M), ±10%(K), ±5%(J). |
| 4 | Saturation Current (Isat) | `saturation_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 5 | Demoted for RF applications — signal inductors carry small currents. Still verify, but not a primary concern. |
| 5 | Rated Current (Irms) | `rated_current` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | The replacement must handle at least the same RMS current. Irms is the thermal rating — exceeding it causes excessive temperature rise. |
| 6 | DC Resistance (DCR) | `dcr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Lower DCR means less I²R loss and less heat. Critical for high-current power inductors. Directly impacts converter efficiency. |
| 7 | Core Material | `core_material` | Identity (exact match) | 5 | Air core, ceramic core, or thin-film only. NOT ferrite — ferrite has excessive losses at RF frequencies. Must match exactly. |
| 8 | Shielding | `shielding` | Application review (manual) | 8 | Shielding trade-offs differ at RF. Shielded inductors may have lower Q due to eddy currents in shield. Verify based on circuit sensitivity and coupling concerns. |
| 9 | Self-Resonant Frequency (SRF) | `srf` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | Must be ≥10× operating frequency for stable inductive behavior. Critical for RF — below SRF the inductor becomes capacitive. Higher SRF is always better. |
| 10 | Operating Temp Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | The replacement must cover at least the full operating temperature range of the original. |
| 11 | Height (Seated Max) | `height` | Fit (physical ≤) | 5 | Critical for tight enclosures and low-profile designs. Power inductors vary significantly in height. |
| 12 | AC Resistance (ACR) | `acr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 4 | Lower AC resistance means less loss at the switching frequency. Important for high-frequency converters. |
| 13 | Inductance vs DC Bias | `inductance_vs_dc_bias` | Application review (manual) | 7 | Inductance drops as DC current increases. Different core materials have different L vs I curves. Ferrite has hard saturation; metal alloy has soft roll-off. Consult datasheets. |
| 14 | Construction Type | `construction_type` | Identity (exact match) | 4 | Construction (wound, multilayer, molded) affects electrical and thermal characteristics. Wound types have higher current; multilayer types are smaller but lower current. |
| 15 | AEC-Q200 Qualification | `aec_q200` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Required for automotive applications. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one. |
| 16 | Moisture Sensitivity Level | `msl` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 3 | MSL 1 (unlimited floor life) is best. Lower MSL number is less restrictive and always acceptable. |
| 17 | Packaging | `packaging` | Operational (non-electrical) | 2 | Tape & Reel required for automated pick-and-place. Ensure reel width and pitch match feeder specs. |
| 18 | Q Factor (Quality Factor) | `q_factor` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 9 | PRIMARY specification for RF inductors. Higher Q = lower losses = better selectivity in tuned circuits. Replacement must meet or exceed original Q at the operating frequency. |
| 19 | Inductance Tolerance | `inductance_tolerance` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Standard: ±2%, ±5%, ±10%. Critical for tuned circuits and filters where inductance directly sets the frequency response. Tighter is always better. |

### B1 — Rectifier Diodes — Standard, Fast, and Ultrafast Recovery

- **Category:** Discrete Semiconductors
- **Attributes (rules):** 23
- **Logic last updated:** 2026-02-19
- **Description:** Hard logic filters for rectifier diode replacement part validation

| # | Attribute | Attribute ID | Match Logic | Weight | Engineering Reason |
|---|-----------|--------------|-------------|:------:|--------------------|
| 1 | Recovery Category | `recovery_category` | Identity upgrade (match or superior) | 10 | Recovery category reflects how quickly the diode stops conducting reverse current. Hierarchy: Ultrafast (<50ns trr) > Fast (50-500ns) > Standard (>500ns). Upgrading is allowed (faster is always safe); downgrading is not — a standard diode in a high-frequency switching supply causes massive reverse current pulses, power dissipation, and potential thermal failure. _(Hierarchy best→worst: Ultrafast > Fast > Standard)_ |
| 2 | Max Repetitive Peak Reverse Voltage (Vrrm) | `vrrm` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 10 | Primary voltage specification. The maximum repetitive reverse voltage the diode can block without breakdown. Higher is always safe. Do NOT confuse Vrrm with Vdc — Vrrm covers repetitive pulsed reverse voltage. |
| 3 | Max DC Blocking Voltage (Vdc) | `vdc` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 8 | Maximum continuous DC reverse voltage. Usually equal to or slightly lower than Vrrm. Relevant for circuits with sustained reverse bias such as reverse polarity protection. |
| 4 | Average Rectified Forward Current (Io) | `io_avg` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 10 | Primary current specification. Maximum average forward current at a specified reference temperature. Higher is always acceptable. Compare at the same reference temperature (Tc or Ta). |
| 5 | Forward Voltage Drop (Vf) | `vf` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 8 | Voltage across the diode when conducting. Lower is better — Vf determines conduction power loss (P = Vf x If). In low-voltage circuits (5V, 3.3V), Vf has an outsized impact on efficiency. |
| 6 | Max Surge Forward Current (Ifsm) | `ifsm` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | Maximum non-repetitive peak forward current for a single half-sine pulse (8.3ms/60Hz or 10ms/50Hz). This is the startup/inrush current rating. Critical in capacitor-input filters and motor drives. |
| 7 | Reverse Recovery Time (trr) | `trr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 8 | The most critical switching characteristic. During trr the diode conducts reverse current, causing power loss, voltage spikes, and EMI. Standard: >500ns, Fast: 50-500ns, Ultrafast: <50ns. Faster is always better for switching but comes with a Vf trade-off. |
| 8 | Reverse Recovery Charge (Qrr) | `qrr` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 7 | Total charge recovered during reverse recovery — a better indicator of switching loss than trr alone. Two diodes with the same trr can have very different Qrr depending on recovery waveform shape. Lower Qrr means lower switching losses. |
| 9 | Recovery Behavior (Soft vs. Snappy) | `recovery_behavior` | Application review (manual) | 6 | How abruptly reverse current stops during recovery. Snappy recovery generates high di/dt voltage spikes (V = L x di/dt) that can exceed ratings of nearby components and cause EMI. In circuits with significant parasitic inductance, snappy recovery can be destructive. Not all datasheets specify this parameter. |
| 10 | Reverse Leakage Current (Ir) | `ir_leakage` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | Current flowing when reverse-biased. Lower is better. Important in high-voltage applications (leakage x voltage = standby power), battery-powered circuits, and high-temperature environments where leakage increases exponentially. |
| 11 | Junction Capacitance (Cj) | `cj` | Application review (manual) | 4 | PN junction capacitance when reverse-biased. Irrelevant at 50/60Hz. At high-frequency switching (>100kHz), Cj contributes to switching losses and reverse current spikes. Flag for review if application operates above 100kHz. |
| 12 | Configuration | `configuration` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Critical physical and functional constraint. Configurations: Single, Dual Common Cathode, Dual Common Anode, Dual Series (half-bridge), Bridge (4 diodes). Internal wiring determines pin connections — a common cathode dual cannot replace a common anode dual even if the package is identical. |
| 13 | Package / Form Factor | `package_case` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Must match the PCB footprint. Common packages: SMD (SOD-123, SMA, SMB, SMC, DPAK, D2PAK, PowerDI), Through-hole (DO-41, DO-15, DO-27, DO-201, TO-220, TO-247). Package also determines thermal capability. |
| 14 | Pin Configuration / Polarity Marking | `pin_configuration` | Identity (exact match) | 10 | Incorrect polarity = reverse-biased diode in a forward-biased position = circuit failure. For multi-die packages, pin-to-function mapping varies between manufacturers. The tab/heatsink connection also matters — usually connected to the common pin. |
| 15 | Thermal Resistance, Junction-to-Case (Rtheta_jc) | `rth_jc` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 6 | How effectively the diode transfers heat from junction to case. Lower is better. Dominant thermal metric for heatsink-mounted packages (TO-220, TO-247, DPAK). Tj = Tc + (Pd x Rtheta_jc). |
| 16 | Thermal Resistance, Junction-to-Ambient (Rtheta_ja) | `rth_ja` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≤ original | 5 | How effectively the diode transfers heat to surrounding air without a heatsink. Relevant for SMD packages and small through-hole packages relying on PCB copper for heat dissipation. |
| 17 | Max Junction Temperature (Tj_max) | `tj_max` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 7 | Maximum allowable junction temperature. Standard: 150C or 175C. Higher Tj_max provides more thermal headroom. A replacement with lower Tj_max may overheat in conditions the original survived. |
| 18 | Operating Temperature Range | `operating_temp` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement range ⊇ original | 7 | Ambient temperature range over which the device is rated. The replacement range must fully contain the original range. For automotive: -40C to +125C or +150C. |
| 19 | Power Dissipation (Pd) | `pd` | Threshold (numeric ≥ / ≤ / ⊇) — replacement ≥ original | 6 | Maximum power the device can dissipate. If Vf, Io, and thermal resistance all meet their thresholds, Pd is implicitly satisfied — but it is a useful cross-check, especially for SMD packages. |
| 20 | AEC-Q101 Qualification | `aec_q101` | Identity flag (boolean gate) | 8 | Automotive qualification for discrete semiconductors. AEC-Q101 (not Q200 — Q200 is for passives). Includes HTRB, H3TRB, TC stress tests. A non-qualified part cannot replace a qualified one in automotive applications. |
| 21 | Mounting Style | `mounting_style` | Identity (exact match) | 9 | Surface mount vs. through-hole. Cannot interchange without PCB redesign. Within each: axial vs. vertical (different footprints, mounting hardware). Power pad packages require matching PCB pads for thermal path. |
